<p>After Nas was removed from the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Summer_Jam_(festival)" title="Summer Jam (festival)">Summer Jam</a> lineup due to allegedly planning to perform the song <i><a href="/wiki/Ether_(song)" title="Ether (song)">Ether</a></i> while a mock <a href="/wiki/Lynching" title="Lynching">lynching</a> of a Jay-Z <a href="/wiki/Effigy" title="Effigy">effigy</a> took place behind him, <a href="/wiki/Cam%27ron" title="Cam&#39;ron">Cam'ron</a> was announced as a last minute replacement and headlined the show instead. Nas appeared on <a href="/wiki/Power_105.1" class="mw-redirect" title="Power 105.1">Power 105.1</a> days later and addressed a number of fellow artists, including <a href="/wiki/Nelly" title="Nelly">Nelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noreaga" class="mw-redirect" title="Noreaga">Noreaga</a> and Cam'ron himself.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Nas praised Cam'ron as a good lyricist, but branded his album <i><a href="/wiki/Come_Home_With_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="Come Home With Me">Come Home With Me</a></i> as "wack".<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> After Cam'ron heard of Nas's words, he appeared on <a href="/wiki/Funkmaster_Flex" title="Funkmaster Flex">Funkmaster Flex</a>'s Hot 97 and performed a freestyle diss over the beat to Nas's "<a href="/wiki/Hate_Me_Now" title="Hate Me Now">Hate Me Now</a>", making reference to Nas's mother, baby mother and daughter. Nas did not respond directly but appeared on the radio days later, calling Cam'ron a "dummy" for supposedly being used by Hot 97 to generate ratings. Nas eventually responded on his 2002 album <i><a href="/wiki/God%27s_Son_(album)" title="God&#39;s Son (album)">God's Son</a></i> on the song "Zone Out", claiming Cam'ron had <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_United_States" title="HIV/AIDS in the United States">HIV</a>. Cam'ron and the rest of <a href="/wiki/The_Diplomats" title="The Diplomats">The Diplomats</a>, specifically <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones_(rapper)" title="Jim Jones (rapper)">Jim Jones</a> continued to attack Nas throughout 2003, on numerous <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtapes</a>, albums and radio freestyles, however, the feud between the two slowly died down and they eventually reconciled in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2Pac">2Pac</span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/2Pac" class="mw-redirect" title="2Pac">2Pac</a> interpreted lines directed to the <a href="/wiki/Notorious_B.I.G." class="mw-redirect" title="Notorious B.I.G.">Notorious B.I.G.</a> on Nas's 1996 album <i><a href="/wiki/It_Was_Written" title="It Was Written">It Was Written</a></i> to be aimed towards him, he attacked Nas on the track "Against All Odds" from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Don_Killuminati:_The_7_Day_Theory" title="The Don Killuminati: The 7 Day Theory">The Don Killuminati: The 7 Day Theory</a></i>. Nas himself later admitted he was brought to tears when he heard the diss because he idolized 2Pac.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The two later met in <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> before the <a href="/wiki/1996_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1996 MTV Video Music Awards">1996 MTV Video Music Awards</a> and ended their feud, with 2Pac promising to remove any disses aimed at Nas from the official album release; however, 2Pac was shot four times in <a href="/wiki/Murder_of_Tupac_Shakur" title="Murder of Tupac Shakur">a drive-by shooting</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, three days later on September 7, dying of his wounds on September 13, before any edits to <a href="/wiki/The_Don_Killuminati:_The_7_Day_Theory" title="The Don Killuminati: The 7 Day Theory">the album</a> could be made.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Young_Jeezy">Young Jeezy</span></h3>
<p>After Nas blamed <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">Southern hip hop</a> as the cause of the perceived artistic decline of the genre on his 2006 single "<a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Is_Dead_(song)" title="Hip Hop Is Dead (song)">Hip Hop Is Dead</a>", from the <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Is_Dead" title="Hip Hop Is Dead">album of the same name</a>, his then-<a href="/wiki/Def_Jam" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam">Def Jam</a> labelmate <a href="/wiki/Young_Jeezy" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Jeezy">Young Jeezy</a> took offense by claiming that Nas had "no street credibility" and vowing his album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Inspiration" class="mw-redirect" title="The Inspiration">The Inspiration</a></i> would outsell <i>Hip Hop is Dead</i>, which were released one week apart from each other in December 2006. After failing to do so,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Young Jeezy took back his disses towards Nas, and the two later collaborated on the 2008 hit single "<a href="/wiki/My_President" title="My President">My President</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bill_O.27Reilly_and_Virginia_Tech_controversy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bill_O'Reilly_and_Virginia_Tech_controversy">Bill O'Reilly and Virginia Tech controversy</span></h3>
<p>On September 6, 2007, Nas performed at a free concert for the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech" title="Virginia Tech">Virginia Tech</a> student body and faculty, following the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech_shooting" title="Virginia Tech shooting">school shooting there</a>. He was joined by <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Jackson" title="Alan Jackson">Alan Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Vassar" title="Phil Vassar">Phil Vassar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews_Band" title="Dave Matthews Band">Dave Matthews Band</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vt.edu_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vt.edu-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> When announced that Nas was to perform, political commentator <a href="/wiki/Bill_O%27Reilly_(political_commentator)" title="Bill O&#39;Reilly (political commentator)">Bill O'Reilly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> denounced the concert and called for Nas's removal, citing "violent" lyrics on songs such as "Shoot 'Em Up", "Got Urself a Gun", and "Made You Look". During his "Talking Points Memo" segment for August 15, 2007, an argument erupted in which O'Reilly claimed that it was not only Nas's lyrical content that made him inappropriate for the event, citing the gun conviction on Nas's <a href="/wiki/Criminal_record" title="Criminal record">criminal record</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 6, 2007, during his set at "A Concert for Virginia Tech", Nas twice referred to Bill O'Reilly as "a chump", prompting loud cheers by members of the crowd. About two weeks later, Nas was interviewed by Shaheem Reid of MTV News, where he criticised O'Reilly, calling him uncivilized and willing to go to extremes for publicity.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Responding to O'Reilly, Nas, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a>, said:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>He doesn't understand the younger generation. He deals with the past. The people he represents are Republican, older, a generation that has nothing to do with the reality of what's happening now with my generation. ... He's not really on my radar. People like him are supposed to be taught and people like me are supposed to let niggas like him know. I don't take him serious. His shit is all about getting facts twisted or whatever. I wouldn't honor anything Bill O'Reilly has to say. It just shows you what bloodsuckers like him do: They abuse something like the Virginia Tech tragedy for show ratings. You can't talk to a person like that.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>On July 23, 2008, Nas appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colbert_Report" title="The Colbert Report">The Colbert Report</a></i> to discuss his opinion of O'Reilly and Fox News, which he accused of <a href="/wiki/Media_bias" title="Media bias">bias</a> against the African-American community and re-challenged O'Reilly to a debate.<sup id="cite_ref-Colbert_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colbert-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> During the appearance, Nas sat on boxes of more than 625,000 signatures gathered by online advocacy organisation <a href="/wiki/Color_of_Change" title="Color of Change">Color of Change</a> in support of a petition accusing Fox of <a href="/wiki/Race_baiting" class="mw-redirect" title="Race baiting">race-baiting</a> and fear-mongering.<sup id="cite_ref-Colbert_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colbert-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lijadu_Sisters">Lijadu Sisters</span></h3>
<p>On his 2006 mixtape, <i>The Prophecy, Vol 2: The Beginning of the N,</i> Nas had a track titled "Life's Gone Low". It was a substantial sampling of "Life's Gone Down Low", a song released by Nigerian musician twin <a href="/wiki/Lijadu_Sisters" title="Lijadu Sisters">Lijadu Sisters</a> in their 1976 <i>Danger</i> album.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Nas lifted vocal <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hooks</a> and the entire beats from the duo's work. Nas neither obtained clearance nor did he credit the Sisters for the reuse. Reacting to the issue, the Lijadu Sisters were reported to have said: "We can't forgive him," but "If other people want to use your stuff, that tells that you did something good."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doja_Cat">Doja Cat</span></h3>
<p>In 2020, after <a href="/wiki/Doja_Cat" title="Doja Cat">Doja Cat</a> faced accusations of participating in racist conversations on the internet, Nas referenced her in his song "<a href="/wiki/Ultra_Black_(Nas_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra Black (Nas song)">Ultra Black</a>"; in the song, Nas describes himself as "unapologetically black, the opposite of Doja Cat". The response to the lyric was mixed, with some defending his right to criticize her, and others resurfacing allegations that he verbally abused his ex-wife, <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Doja Cat shrugged off the namedrop, jokingly referencing the lyric in a <a href="/wiki/TikTok" title="TikTok">TikTok</a> video.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>, Doja Cat said that she has no interest in "beefing" with Nas saying  "I fucking love Nas, thank fucking god he noticed me. I love Nas. So I don't give a shit. He can say whatever he wants. I really don't care".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Nas later claimed that the line was not meant to be perceived as a "diss", and that he was "just trying to find another word that worked with the scheme of the song."<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_ventures">Business ventures</span></h2>
<p>On April 10, 2013, Nas invested an undisclosed six-figure sum into <a href="/wiki/Mass_Appeal_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass Appeal Magazine"><i>Mass Appeal</i> magazine</a>, where he went on to serve as the publication's associate publisher, joined by creative firm Decon and White Owl Capital Partners.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In June 2013, he opened his own sneaker store.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2013, he invested in a technology startup company, a job search appmaker called Proven.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Nas invested as part of a $2.8M round in viral video startup ViralGains another addition to Queens-bridge venture partners portfolio.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nas has a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Hennessy" title="Hennessy">Hennessy</a> and has been working with their "Wild Rabbit" campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2014, Nas partnered with job placement startup Koru to fund a scholarship for 10 college graduates to go through Koru's training program. Nas will also be joining the startup as a guest coach.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Nas is a co-owner of a Cloud-based service LANDR, an automated, drag-and-drop digital audio postproduction tool which automates "mastering", the final stage in audio production.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In June 2015, Nas joined forces with New York City soul food restaurant Sweet Chick.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> He plans to expand the restaurant brand nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The Los Angeles location opened in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> He owns his own clothing line called HSTRY.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, Nas was paid $40 million after <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> acquired the doorbell company <a href="/wiki/Ring_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ring Inc.">Ring Inc.</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/PillPack" title="PillPack">PillPack</a> – the latter of which he invested in via his investment firm, Queensbridge Venture Partners.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He has continued to invest heavily in technology startups including <a href="/wiki/Dropbox_(service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropbox (service)">Dropbox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robinhood_(Company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robinhood (Company)">Robinhood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Nas is a spokesperson and mentor for P'Tones Records, a non-profit after-school music program with the mission "to create constructive opportunities for urban youth through no-cost music programs."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 15, 1994, Nas's ex-fiancée Carmen Bryan gave birth to their daughter, Destiny.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nas also briefly dated <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, Nas married <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Kelis" title="Kelis">Kelis</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> after a two-year relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> On April 30, 2009, a spokesperson confirmed that Kelis filed for divorce, citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Kelis gave birth to Nas's first son on July 21, 2009, although the event was soured by a disagreement which ended in Nas announcing the birth of his son, Knight, at a gig in <a href="/wiki/Queens,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Queens, New York">Queens, New York</a>, against Kelis's wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The birth was also announced by Nas via an online video.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The couple's divorce was finalized on May 21, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Kelis accused Nas of being <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">physically and mentally abusive</a> during their marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Nas replied to the accusations on social media, accusing Kelis of attempting to slander him in the time of a custody battle and accusing Kelis of abusing his daughter, Destiny.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2012, Nas was involved in a dispute with a concert promoter in <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, having accepted $300,000 for a concert in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, Angola's capital for New Year's Eve and then not showing up. American promoter Patrick Allocco and his son, who arranged for Nas's concert, were detained at gunpoint and taken to an Angolan jail by the local promoter who fronted the $300,000 for the concert. Only after the U.S. Embassy intervened were the promoter and his son allowed to leave jail—but were placed under house arrest at their hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the month Nas had returned all $300,000, and, after 49 days of travel ban, Allocco and his son were both released.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 15, 2012, Nas became the first rapper to have a personal verified account on <a href="/wiki/Genius_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genius (website)">Genius</a>, where he explains his own lyrics and occasionally comments on lyrics from other rappers he admires.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2009 the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> filed a federal <a href="/wiki/Tax_lien" title="Tax lien">tax lien</a> against Nas for over $2.5&#160;million, seeking unpaid taxes dating back to 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> By early 2011 this figure had ballooned to over $6.4&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Early in 2012 reports emerged that the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">IRS</a> had filed papers in Georgia to <a href="/wiki/Garnishment" title="Garnishment">garnish</a> a portion of Nas's earnings from material published under <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music,_Inc." title="Broadcast Music, Inc.">BMI</a> and <a href="/wiki/ASCAP" class="mw-redirect" title="ASCAP">ASCAP</a>, until his delinquent tax bill is settled.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2013, it was announced that Nas would open a sneaker store in Las Vegas called 12&#160;am RUN (pronounced Midnight Run) as part of <a href="/wiki/The_LINQ" class="mw-redirect" title="The LINQ">The LINQ</a> retail development.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> established the Nasir Jones Hip-Hop Fellowship, to fund scholars and artists who show potential and creativity in the arts in connection to hip hop.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an October 2014 episode of <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Finding_Your_Roots" title="Finding Your Roots">Finding Your Roots</a></i>, Nas learned about five generations of his ancestry. His great-great-great-grandmother, Pocahontas Little, was an enslaved woman who was sold for $830. When host <a href="/wiki/Henry_Louis_Gates" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Louis Gates">Henry Louis Gates</a> showed Nas her bill of sale and told him more about the man who bought her, Nas remarked that he is considering buying the land where the slave owner lived. Nas was also shown the marriage certificate of his great-great-great-grandmother, Pocahontas, and great-great-great-grandfather, Calvin.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 12, 2019, Nas was honored by&#160;<i><a href="/wiki/Haute_Living" title="Haute Living">Haute Living</a></i>, along with&#160;<a href="/wiki/Watches_of_Switzerland" title="Watches of Switzerland">Watches of Switzerland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hennessy" title="Hennessy">Hennessy</a>, in a celebratory affair that included a violin rendition of iconic Nas songs performed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_W._Hardy" title="Edward W. Hardy">Edward W. Hardy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nas is a fan of his hometown baseball team the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> and English soccer team <a href="/wiki/Everton_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Everton FC">Everton FC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_Nominations">Awards and Nominations</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammy_Awards">Grammy Awards</span></h3>
<p>The Grammy Awards are held annually by the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Recording_Arts_and_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences">National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences</a>. Nas has won 1 Grammy out of 15 nominations altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1050814317">.mw-parser-output .awards-table td:last-child{text-align:center}</style>
